pattern 1/620: PROVED cells=14 depth=3 diamonds=2 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=1 bridged_hexagons=1 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=0 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=1 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000000000000000001000001010001010100000001100001010010001100001
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Circular ladder {r8c3—r9c3, r8c5—r9c4, r8c8—r9c9}:
      Satellites r6c3 (rung 1), r7c6 (rung 2), r7c7 (rung 3) forced to distinct colors. Add triangle.
  2.  Diamond {r6c5, r6c3, r6c7, r7c7} (spine r6c3—r6c7).
      → color(r6c5) = color(r7c7). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r5c6, [r6c5=r7c7], r7c6, r8c5} (spine [r6c5=r7c7]—r7c6).
      → color(r5c6) = color(r8c5). Identify.
  4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {[r5c6=r8c5], r5c8, r6c7, r6c3, r9c3, r9c4}
      Bridges: r8c8—r8c3 (edges [r5c6=r8c5]—r5c8 ↔ r6c3—r9c3), r4c9—r9c9 (edges r5c8—r6c7 ↔ r9c3—r9c4), [r6c5=r7c7]—r7c6 (edges r6c7—r6c3 ↔ r9c4—[r5c6=r8c5]).
      Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 2/620: PROVED cells=14 depth=3 diamonds=3 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=0 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=1 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000000000000000001000001010001010100001000001001010010010001100
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3, r9c2} (spine r7c3—r8c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c7, [r6c3=r9c2], r9c7, r9c6} (spine [r6c3=r9c2]—r9c7).
      → color(r6c7) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r5c8, r5c6, [r6c7=r9c6], r6c5} (spine r5c6—[r6c7=r9c6]).
      → color(r5c8) = color(r6c5). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r6c3=r9c2], r7c3, r7c9, r9c7}:
      Diagonals: {[r6c3=r9c2], r7c9} and {r7c3, r9c7} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r6c3=r9c2]) = color(r7c9) → forces r4c9 = r7c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r7c3) = color(r9c7) → forces [r5c8=r6c5] = r8c5 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c8, r5c5, r5c6, r6c6} (spine r5c5—r5c6).
      → color(r5c8) = color(r6c6). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {[r5c8=r6c6], r9c6, r9c8, r9c2} (spine r9c6—r9c8).

  3.  SET: {row 5, row 9} − {box 5, box 9}.
      Remainder: {[r5c8=r6c6=r9c2], r9c6} = {[r5c8=r6c6=r9c2], r7c7, r8c9}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  4.  K₄ on {[r5c8=r6c6=r9c2], r7c7, r8c9, r9c8}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 5, row 6} − {box 5, box 6}.
      Remainder: {r6c3} = {r4c9}.
      → color(r6c3) = color(r4c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {[r4c9=r6c3], r9c3, r9c9, r9c5} (spine r9c3—r9c9).
      → color([r4c9=r6c3]) = color(r9c5). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r5c8, [r4c9=r6c3=r9c5], r5c5, r8c5} (spine [r4c9=r6c3=r9c5]—r5c5).
      → color(r5c8) = color(r8c5). Identify.
  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r5c8=r8c5] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {[r4c9=r6c3=r9c5], r6c7, r8c7, r7c8, r7c6} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r7c3, r7c9, r9c7, r9c2}:
      Diagonals: {r7c3, r9c7} and {r7c9, r9c2} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r7c3) = color(r9c7) → forces r6c7 = r9c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r7c9) = color(r9c2) → forces r4c9 = r7c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c4). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r6c7, [r5c8=r6c4], r6c3, [r8c3=r9c4]} (spine [r5c8=r6c4]—r6c3).
      → color(r6c7) = color([r8c3=r9c4]). Identify.
  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c7=r8c3=r9c4] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r4c9, [r5c8=r6c4], r7c4, r7c7, r8c9} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9}
      row 6 {r6c3, r6c5, [r6c8=r7c9]}
      row 8 {r8c3, r8c5, r8c7}

      4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

            row 6 {r6c3, r6c5, [r6c8=r7c9=r8c4]}
            row 8 {r8c3, [r6c8=r7c9=r8c4], r8c7}
            row 9 {r9c2, r9c6, r9c7}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (col, box, box); row 6↔row 8 (col, box, box); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, col)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Case B: color([r6c8=r7c9]) ≠ color(r8c4). Add edge.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r8c3, r8c4, r9c6, r9c2}:
            Diagonals: {r8c3, r9c6} and {r8c4, r9c2} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r8c3) = color(r9c6) → forces r5c6 = r9c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r8c4) = color(r9c2) → forces [r6c8=r7c9] = r8c4 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c8, r4c9, r5c9, r9c9} (spine r4c9—r5c9).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r9c9). Identify.
  2.  Branch on r4c9, r9c4:
      Case A: color(r4c9) = color(r9c4). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c6, r5c9, [r6c8=r9c9], r6c5}:
            Diagonals: {r5c6, [r6c8=r9c9]} and {r5c9, r6c5} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c6) = color([r6c8=r9c9]) → forces r5c6 = r7c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r5c9) = color(r6c5) → forces r8c3 = r9c2 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r4c9) ≠ color(r9c4). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c9, r5c9, r5c3, r8c3, r8c5, r9c4}
            Bridges: [r6c8=r9c9]—r8c7 (edges r4c9—r5c9 ↔ r8c3—r8c5), r5c6—r7c6 (edges r5c9—r5c3 ↔ r8c5—r9c4), r6c3—[r6c8=r9c9] (edges r5c3—r8c3 ↔ r9c4—r4c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Case B: color(r4c9) ≠ color(r8c4). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c9, r5c9, r5c3, r9c3, r9c4, r8c4}
            Bridges: [r6c8=r8c9]—r9c7 (edges r4c9—r5c9 ↔ r9c3—r9c4), r5c6—r7c6 (edges r5c9—r5c3 ↔ r9c4—r8c4), r6c3—[r6c8=r8c9] (edges r5c3—r9c3 ↔ r8c4—r4c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c8, r4c9, r5c9, r8c9} (spine r4c9—r5c9).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r8c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {[r6c8=r8c9], r7c7, r7c8, r7c6} (spine r7c7—r7c8).
      → color([r6c8=r8c9]) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9, [r6c8=r7c6=r8c9]} (spine r5c6—r5c9).
      → color(r5c3) = color([r6c8=r7c6=r8c9]). Identify.
  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r5c3=r6c8=r7c6=r8c9] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r6c3, r6c5, r8c5, r9c4, r9c3} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

            Bridges: r8c9—r8c2 (edges r4c9—r5c9 ↔ r7c3—r9c1), r5c6—r9c6 (edges r5c9—r5c3 ↔ r9c1—r9c8), r6c3—r6c8 (edges r5c3—r7c3 ↔ r9c8—r4c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

        2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c3, [r5c6=r8c5], r6c5, r6c2}:
            Diagonals: {r5c3, r6c5} and {[r5c6=r8c5], r6c2} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c3) = color(r6c5) → forces r5c3 = r9c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color([r5c6=r8c5]) = color(r6c2) → forces [r5c6=r8c5] = r8c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r5c6) ≠ color(r8c5). Add edge.
        3.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c9, r5c8, r5c6, r8c5, r9c5, r9c9}
            Bridges: r6c8—r6c5 (edges r4c9—r5c8 ↔ r8c5—r9c5), r5c3—r9c3 (edges r5c8—r5c6 ↔ r9c5—r9c9), r7c6—r7c9 (edges r5c6—r8c5 ↔ r9c9—r4c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r4c9, r8c7:
      Case A: color(r4c9) = color(r8c7). Identify.
        2.  Parity transport:
            row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c8}
            row 6 {r6c2, r6c5, r6c7}
            row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, [r4c9=r8c7]}
            row 9 {r9c2, r9c5, r9c8}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (box, box, box); row 5↔row 8 (col, col, box); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Case B: color(r4c9) ≠ color(r8c7). Add edge.
        3.  Diamond {r6c7, r4c9, r8c7, r7c9} (spine r4c9—r8c7).

            row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, r8c7}
            row 9 {r9c2, r9c5, r9c8}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (box, box, box); row 6↔row 9 (col, col, box); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Case B: color(r4c9) ≠ color(r5c3). Add edge.
        6.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c3, r5c6, r6c5, r6c2}:
            Diagonals: {r5c3, r6c5} and {r5c6, r6c2} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c3) = color(r6c5) → forces r4c9 = r5c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r5c6) = color(r6c2) → forces r4c9 = r9c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 107/620: PROVED cells=14 depth=2 diamonds=1 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=1 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=1 branches=1 complete=true greedy_branches=1 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000000000000000001001001010010010100000001100000100001010001001
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c6, r7c6, r9c6, r8c4} (spine r7c6—r9c6).
      → color(r5c6) = color(r8c4). Identify.
  2.  Branch on r6c5, r7c6:
      Case A: color(r6c5) = color(r7c6). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c3, [r5c6=r8c4], [r6c5=r7c6], r6c2}:
            Diagonals: {r5c3, [r6c5=r7c6]} and {[r5c6=r8c4], r6c2} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c3) = color([r6c5=r7c6]) → forces [r6c5=r7c6] = r7c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color([r5c6=r8c4]) = color(r6c2) → forces r6c2 = r9c2 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r6c5) ≠ color(r7c6). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c9, r6c7, r6c5, r7c6, r9c6, r9c9}
            Bridges: r5c8—[r5c6=r8c4] (edges r4c9—r6c7 ↔ r7c6—r9c6), r6c2—r9c2 (edges r6c7—r6c5 ↔ r9c6—r9c9), [r5c6=r8c4]—r8c9 (edges r6c5—r7c6 ↔ r9c9—r4c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r4c6, r9c5:
      Case A: color(r4c6) = color(r9c5). Identify.
        2.  Diamond {r6c6, [r4c6=r9c5], r5c5, r8c5} (spine [r4c6=r9c5]—r5c5).
            → color(r6c6) = color(r8c5). Identify.
        3.  Diamond {r4c9, [r4c6=r9c5], r9c9, r9c3} (spine [r4c6=r9c5]—r9c9).
            → color(r4c9) = color(r9c3). Identify.
        4.  Odd wheel: hub r6c8 forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {[r4c9=r9c3], r5c8, r8c8, [r6c6=r8c5], r6c3} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r4c6) ≠ color(r9c5). Add edge.
        5.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c6, r6c6, r6c8, r8c8, r9c9, r9c5}
            Bridges: r7c6—r7c9 (edges r4c6—r6c6 ↔ r8c8—r9c9), r6c3—r9c3 (edges r6c6—r6c8 ↔ r9c9—r9c5), r5c8—r5c5 (edges r6c8—r8c8 ↔ r9c5—r4c6).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

            → color(r6c8) = color(r7c6). Identify.
        3.  Diamond {[r6c8=r7c6], r4c9, r7c9, r9c9} (spine r4c9—r7c9).
            → color([r6c8=r7c6]) = color(r9c9). Identify.
        4.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c8=r7c6=r9c9] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {[r4c6=r6c3], r4c9, r7c9, r8c7, r8c4, r9c4, r9c3} (length 7) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r4c6) ≠ color(r6c3). Add edge.
        5.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r4c6, r4c9, r5c8, r5c5}:
            Diagonals: {r4c6, r5c8} and {r4c9, r5c5} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r4c6) = color(r5c8) → forces r4c6 = r6c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r4c9) = color(r5c5) → forces r6c3 = r9c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:

      → color(r4c9) = color(r8c8). Identify.
  2.  Branch on r5c8, r8c2:
      Case A: color(r5c8) = color(r8c2). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r4c9=r8c8], [r5c8=r8c2], r7c3, r7c9}:
            Diagonals: {[r4c9=r8c8], r7c3} and {[r5c8=r8c2], r7c9} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color([r4c9=r8c8]) = color(r7c3) → forces r6c3 = r7c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.

            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

            Case 2: color([r4c9=r7c8]) = color(r5c5) → forces r5c5 = r8c5 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r4c6) ≠ color(r9c7). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c6, r6c6, r6c3, r8c3, r8c9, r9c7}
            Bridges: r5c5—r8c5 (edges r4c6—r6c6 ↔ r8c3—r8c9), r6c8—[r4c9=r7c8] (edges r6c6—r6c3 ↔ r8c9—r9c7), r7c3—[r4c9=r7c8] (edges r6c3—r8c3 ↔ r9c7—r4c6).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r5c8, [r5c5=r8c6], r8c8, r8c3} (spine [r5c5=r8c6]—r8c8).
      → color(r5c8) = color(r8c3). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r4c9, r6c7, r9c7, r7c9}:
      Diagonals: {r4c9, r9c7} and {r6c7, r7c9} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r4c9) = color(r9c7) → forces r9c2 = r9c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r6c7) = color(r7c9) → forces r7c3 = r7c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r5c5) = color(r8c6). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3, r9c2} (spine r7c3—r8c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  3.  Circular ladder {[r5c5=r8c6]—r6c6, r8c3—[r6c3=r9c2], r8c7—r6c7}:
      Satellites r4c6 (rung 1), r7c3 (rung 2) forced to distinct colors. Add edge.

        → via rows {4, 6} [even]
      col 6 {r4c6, [r5c5=r8c6], r6c6}
        → via rows {6, 8} [even]
      Cycle parity: odd. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r4c9, r7c9, r9c9, r8c8} (spine r7c9—r9c9).
      → color(r4c9) = color(r8c8). Identify.
  2.  Branch on r5c8, r8c2:
      Case A: color(r5c8) = color(r8c2). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r4c9=r8c8], [r5c8=r8c2], r7c3, r7c9}:
            Diagonals: {[r4c9=r8c8], r7c3} and {[r5c8=r8c2], r7c9} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color([r4c9=r8c8]) = color(r7c3) → forces r6c3 = r7c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color([r5c8=r8c2]) = color(r7c9) → forces r5c5 = [r5c8=r8c2] (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r5c8) ≠ color(r8c2). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r5c8, r6c7, r6c6, r9c6, r9c1, r8c2}
            Bridges: [r4c9=r8c8]—r9c9 (edges r5c8—r6c7 ↔ r9c6—r9c1), r6c3—r7c3 (edges r6c7—r6c6 ↔ r9c1—r8c2), r4c6—[r4c9=r8c8] (edges r6c6—r9c6 ↔ r8c2—r5c8).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r6c3, r6c6, r8c6, r8c3}:
      Diagonals: {r6c3, r8c6} and {r6c6, r8c3} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r6c3) = color(r8c6) → forces r3c8 = r3c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r6c6) = color(r8c3) → forces r5c9 = r9c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c9, r5c5, r5c6, r6c6} (spine r5c5—r5c6).
      → color(r5c9) = color(r6c6). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r8c3, r9c1, r9c2, r9c9} (spine r9c1—r9c2).
      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c9). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r6c8, [r5c9=r6c6], r6c3, [r8c3=r9c9]} (spine [r5c9=r6c6]—r6c3).
      → color(r6c8) = color([r8c3=r9c9]). Identify.
  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c8=r8c3=r9c9] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r3c8, r3c9, [r5c9=r6c6], r8c6, r8c8} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

000000000000000000000000011000000000001001001001010010000001010000010001001000100
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r5c6, r6c8:
      Case A: color(r5c6) = color(r6c8). Identify.
        2.  Diamond {[r5c6=r6c8], r5c3, r6c3, r9c3} (spine r5c3—r6c3).
            → color([r5c6=r6c8]) = color(r9c3). Identify.
        3.  Diamond {[r5c6=r6c8=r9c3], r7c8, r9c7, r8c9} (spine r7c8—r9c7).
            → color([r5c6=r6c8=r9c3]) = color(r8c9). Identify.
        4.  Odd wheel: hub [r5c6=r6c8=r8c9=r9c3] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {r3c8, r3c9, r5c9, r5c3, r6c3, r6c5, r8c5, r7c6, r7c8} (length 9) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r5c6) ≠ color(r6c8). Add edge.
        5.  Diamond {r5c9, r5c6, r6c8, r6c5} (spine r5c6—r6c8).
            → color(r5c9) = color(r6c5). Identify.
        6.  Diamond {[r5c9=r6c5], r5c3, r6c3, r9c3} (spine r5c3—r6c3).
            → color([r5c9=r6c5]) = color(r9c3). Identify.
        7.  Diamond {[r5c9=r6c5=r9c3], r8c9, r9c7, r7c8} (spine r8c9—r9c7).
            → color([r5c9=r6c5=r9c3]) = color(r7c8). Identify.
        8.  Odd wheel: hub [r5c9=r6c5=r7c8=r9c3] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {r3c8, r3c9, r8c9, r8c5, r7c6, r5c6, r6c8} (length 7) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 177/620: PROVED cells=14 depth=2 diamonds=1 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=0 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=2 pigeonhole_xwings=0 branches=1 complete=true greedy_branches=1 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=2 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000000011000000000001001001010010010000000000001001010010010001
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r3c8, r5c9:
      Case A: color(r3c8) = color(r5c9). Identify.
        2.  Parity transport:
            row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, [r3c8=r5c9]}
            row 6 {r6c2, r6c5, r6c8}
            row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, r8c8}
            row 9 {r9c2, r9c5, r9c9}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (box, box, box); row 5↔row 8 (col, col, box); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Case B: color(r3c8) ≠ color(r5c9). Add edge.
        3.  Diamond {r3c9, r3c8, r5c9, r6c8} (spine r3c8—r5c9).
            → color(r3c9) = color(r6c8). Identify.
        4.  Parity transport:
            row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9}
            row 6 {r6c2, r6c5, [r3c9=r6c8]}
            row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, r8c8}
            row 9 {r9c2, r9c5, r9c9}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (box, box, box); row 6↔row 9 (col, col, box); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r3c8, r5c8, r9c8, [r5c6=r9c5]} (spine r5c8—r9c8).

      Remainder: {[r3c8=r5c6=r9c5], r9c8} = {[r3c8=r5c6=r9c5], r4c9, r6c7}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 6, row 8} − {col 3, col 8}.
      Remainder: {r6c9, r8c5} = {r5c8, r7c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r6c3, r6c9, r8c5, r8c3}:
      Diagonals: {r6c3, r8c5} and {r6c9, r8c3} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r6c3) = color(r8c5) → forces r3c6 = r3c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r6c9) = color(r8c3) → forces r5c8 = r6c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c8, r6c7, r6c9, r6c3} (spine r6c7—r6c9).
      → color(r5c8) = color(r6c3). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {[r5c8=r6c3], r7c3, r8c3, r9c2} (spine r7c3—r8c3).
      → color([r5c8=r6c3]) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 6, row 9} − {box 6, box 8}.
      Remainder: {[r5c8=r6c3=r9c2], r9c9} = {[r5c8=r6c3=r9c2], r7c6, r8c5}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  4.  K₄ on {[r5c8=r6c3=r9c2], r7c6, r8c5, r9c6}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r8c3, r9c2, r9c3, r9c8} (spine r9c2—r9c3).
      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c8). Identify.
  2.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r5c9, r6c8, r6c6, r8c6, r8c7, r7c9}
      Bridges: r5c8—[r8c3=r9c8] (edges r5c9—r6c8 ↔ r8c6—r8c7), r6c3—[r8c3=r9c8] (edges r6c8—r6c6 ↔ r8c7—r7c9), r3c6—r3c9 (edges r6c6—r8c6 ↔ r7c9—r5c9).
      Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  Branch on r8c5, r9c8:

        2.  Diamond {r8c9, r8c3, [r8c5=r9c8], r9c2} (spine r8c3—[r8c5=r9c8]).
            → color(r8c9) = color(r9c2). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c8, r6c7, r7c7, [r8c5=r9c8]}:
            Diagonals: {r5c8, r7c7} and {r6c7, [r8c5=r9c8]} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c8) = color(r7c7) → forces r6c3 = r8c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r6c7) = color([r8c5=r9c8]) → forces r3c6 = r3c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r8c5) ≠ color(r9c8). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r5c9, r6c7, r6c6, r9c6, r8c5, r8c9}
            Bridges: r5c8—r9c8 (edges r5c9—r6c7 ↔ r9c6—r8c5), r6c3—r8c3 (edges r6c7—r6c6 ↔ r8c5—r8c9), r3c6—r3c9 (edges r6c6—r9c6 ↔ r8c9—r5c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  4.  K₄ on {r3c9, r5c8, [r6c9=r8c8], r7c9}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {col 8, col 9} − {box 6, box 9}.
      Remainder: {r3c9} = {r8c7}.
      → color(r3c9) = color(r8c7). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {[r3c9=r8c7], r3c6, r8c6, r5c6} (spine r3c6—r8c6).
      → color([r3c9=r8c7]) = color(r5c6). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r3c9=r5c6=r8c7], r8c6, r9c5, r9c8}:
      Diagonals: {[r3c9=r5c6=r8c7], r9c5} and {r8c6, r9c8} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r3c9=r5c6=r8c7]) = color(r9c5) → forces [r3c9=r5c6=r8c7] = r5c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c6) = color(r9c8) → forces r6c3 = r6c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Remainder: {[r6c3=r9c2]} = {r3c9, r5c8}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Odd wheel: hub r6c9 forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r3c9, r5c8, r6c8, [r6c3=r9c2], r9c9} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c9, r5c8, r6c8, r8c8} (spine r5c8—r6c8).
      → color(r6c9) = color(r8c8). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c3, [r6c9=r8c8], r8c3, r8c5} (spine [r6c9=r8c8]—r8c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r8c5). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 6, row 8} − {box 6, box 7}.
      Remainder: {[r6c3=r8c5], [r6c9=r8c8]} = {r5c8, r7c3, r9c2}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c8, r6c8, [r6c3=r8c5], r7c3}:
      Diagonals: {r5c8, [r6c3=r8c5]} and {r6c8, r7c3} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r5c8) = color([r6c3=r8c5]) → forces r5c8 = r9c2 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r6c8) = color(r7c3) → forces r7c3 = r8c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r8c6, r9c4, r9c5, r9c3} (spine r9c4—r9c5).
      → color(r8c6) = color(r9c3). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r3c6, r5c6, [r8c6=r9c3], [r5c8=r6c3]} (spine r5c6—[r8c6=r9c3]).
      → color(r3c6) = color([r5c8=r6c3]). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r3c6=r5c8=r6c3], r3c9, r8c9, [r8c6=r9c3]}:
      Diagonals: {[r3c6=r5c8=r6c3], r8c9} and {r3c9, [r8c6=r9c3]} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r3c6=r5c8=r6c3]) = color(r8c9) → forces r7c7 = r8c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r3c9) = color([r8c6=r9c3]) → forces r6c7 = r7c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c8, r6c7, r6c9, r6c3} (spine r6c7—r6c9).
      → color(r5c8) = color(r6c3). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 7, row 9} − {box 7, box 9}.
      Remainder: {r7c6} = {r8c3}.
      → color(r7c6) = color(r8c3). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r3c6, r5c6, [r7c6=r8c3], [r5c8=r6c3]} (spine r5c6—[r7c6=r8c3]).
      → color(r3c6) = color([r5c8=r6c3]). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r3c6=r5c8=r6c3], r3c9, r7c9, [r7c6=r8c3]}:
      Diagonals: {[r3c6=r5c8=r6c3], r7c9} and {r3c9, [r7c6=r8c3]} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r3c6=r5c8=r6c3]) = color(r7c9) → forces r7c9 = r9c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r3c9) = color([r7c6=r8c3]) → forces r6c7 = r9c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  3.  Diamond {r3c6, r5c6, r9c6, [r5c8=r6c3=r9c2]} (spine r5c6—r9c6).
      → color(r3c6) = color([r5c8=r6c3=r9c2]). Identify.
  4.  SET: {col 7, col 9} − {box 6, box 9}.
      Remainder: {r3c9} = {[r3c6=r5c8=r6c3=r9c2]}.
      → color(r3c9) = color([r3c6=r5c8=r6c3=r9c2]), but they share a house. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r5c8) = color(r6c3). Identify.
  2.  Circular ladder {r7c3—r7c8, r8c3—r8c7, r9c2—r9c9}:
      Satellites [r5c8=r6c3] (rung 1), r8c6 (rung 2) forced to distinct colors. Add edge.
  3.  Diamond {r3c6, r5c6, r8c6, [r5c8=r6c3]} (spine r5c6—r8c6).
      → color(r3c6) = color([r5c8=r6c3]). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r3c6=r5c8=r6c3], r7c8, r8c7, r8c6}:
      Diagonals: {[r3c6=r5c8=r6c3], r8c7} and {r7c8, r8c6} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r3c6=r5c8=r6c3]) = color(r8c7) → forces [r3c6=r5c8=r6c3] = r3c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r7c8) = color(r8c6) → forces r7c3 = r7c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  Diamond {r5c6, r5c7, r5c8, r6c9} (spine r5c7—r5c8).
      → color(r5c6) = color(r6c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r3c9, r3c6, [r5c6=r6c9], r9c6} (spine r3c6—[r5c6=r6c9]).
      → color(r3c9) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3, r9c2} (spine r7c3—r8c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r3c9=r9c6] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {[r5c6=r6c9], [r6c3=r9c2], r9c4, r8c5, r8c9} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c6, r5c7, r5c8, r6c9} (spine r5c7—r5c8).
      → color(r5c6) = color(r6c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r3c9, r3c6, [r5c6=r6c9], r8c6} (spine r3c6—[r5c6=r6c9]).
      → color(r3c9) = color(r8c6). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {[r5c6=r6c9], [r3c9=r8c6], r7c9, r8c8} (spine [r3c9=r8c6]—r7c9).
      → color([r5c6=r6c9]) = color(r8c8). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r5c6=r6c9=r8c8], r8c3, r9c2, r9c8}:
      Diagonals: {[r5c6=r6c9=r8c8], r9c2} and {r8c3, r9c8} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r5c6=r6c9=r8c8]) = color(r9c2) → forces [r5c6=r6c9=r8c8] = r6c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c3) = color(r9c8) → forces r7c9 = r9c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c5, r8c5, r9c5, r7c6} (spine r8c5—r9c5).
      → color(r5c5) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  2.  Branch on r7c9, r9c3:
      Case A: color(r7c9) = color(r9c3). Identify.
        3.  Diamond {r3c9, [r7c9=r9c3], r9c9, r9c5} (spine [r7c9=r9c3]—r9c9).
            → color(r3c9) = color(r9c5). Identify.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r3c6, [r3c9=r9c5], r9c9, r8c8, r6c8, r6c6}
            Bridges: [r5c5=r7c6]—r5c8 (edges r3c6—[r3c9=r9c5] ↔ r8c8—r6c8), [r7c9=r9c3]—r6c3 (edges [r3c9=r9c5]—r9c9 ↔ r6c8—r6c6), [r7c9=r9c3]—[r5c5=r7c6] (edges r9c9—r8c8 ↔ r6c6—r3c6).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r7c9) ≠ color(r9c3). Add edge.
        5.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r5c5=r7c6], r7c9, r8c8, r8c5}:
            Diagonals: {[r5c5=r7c6], r8c8} and {r7c9, r8c5} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color([r5c5=r7c6]) = color(r8c8) → forces r6c3 = r9c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r7c9) = color(r8c5) → forces r7c9 = r9c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r5c3) = color(r9c2) → forces [r6c8=r9c9] = r9c2 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r6c2) = color(r8c3) → forces r8c3 = r8c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9}
      row 6 {r6c2, r6c5, r6c8}

      4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.

  3.  Diamond {[r3c6=r7c5], [r3c9=r6c8], r6c5, r6c3} (spine [r3c9=r6c8]—r6c5).
      → color([r3c6=r7c5]) = color(r6c3). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r8c6, r8c8, r9c7, r9c6}:
      Diagonals: {r8c6, r9c7} and {r8c8, r9c6} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r8c6) = color(r9c7) → forces [r3c6=r6c3=r7c5] = r8c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c8) = color(r9c6) → forces [r3c6=r6c3=r7c5] = r9c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Bridges: r5c8—[r8c3=r9c8] (edges r4c9—r6c8 ↔ r8c6—r8c7), r6c3—[r8c3=r9c8] (edges r6c8—r6c6 ↔ r8c7—r7c9), r3c6—r3c9 (edges r6c6—r8c6 ↔ r7c9—r4c9).

000000000000000000000001001000000001000000010001001100001000001010000100010001010
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r7c3, r8c7:
      Case A: color(r7c3) = color(r8c7). Identify.
        2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c8, r6c7, [r7c3=r8c7], r9c8}:
            Diagonals: {r5c8, [r7c3=r8c7]} and {r6c7, r9c8} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c8) = color([r7c3=r8c7]) → forces r6c3 = [r7c3=r8c7] (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r6c7) = color(r9c8) → forces r3c6 = r3c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r7c3) ≠ color(r8c7). Add edge.
        3.  Diamond {r7c9, r7c3, r8c7, r8c2} (spine r7c3—r8c7).
            → color(r7c9) = color(r8c2). Identify.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c9, r6c7, r6c6, r9c6, r9c2, [r7c9=r8c2]}
            Bridges: r5c8—r9c8 (edges r4c9—r6c7 ↔ r9c6—r9c2), r6c3—r7c3 (edges r6c7—r6c6 ↔ r9c2—[r7c9=r8c2]), r3c6—r3c9 (edges r6c6—r9c6 ↔ [r7c9=r8c2]—r4c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Case A: color(r5c8) = color(r9c9). Identify.
        2.  Diamond {r5c6, r5c3, [r5c8=r9c9], r9c3} (spine r5c3—[r5c8=r9c9]).
            → color(r5c6) = color(r9c3). Identify.
        3.  Odd wheel: hub [r5c6=r9c3] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {r5c3, [r5c8=r9c9], r9c5, r6c5, r6c3} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r5c8) ≠ color(r9c9). Add edge.
        4.  Diamond {r3c9, r4c9, r9c9, r5c8} (spine r4c9—r9c9).
            → color(r3c9) = color(r5c8). Identify.
        5.  Diamond {[r3c9=r5c8], r3c6, r5c6, r8c6} (spine r3c6—r5c6).
            → color([r3c9=r5c8]) = color(r8c6). Identify.
        6.  K₄ on {[r3c9=r5c8=r8c6], r7c8, r8c7, r9c9}. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 7, box 9}.
      Remainder: {r8c6} = {r7c3}.
      → color(r8c6) = color(r7c3). Identify.
  2.  SET: {col 8, col 9} − {box 6, box 9}.
      Remainder: {r3c9} = {r8c7}.
      → color(r3c9) = color(r8c7). Identify.
  3.  Odd wheel: hub [r7c3=r8c6] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r3c6, [r3c9=r8c7], r8c3, r6c3, r6c6} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r3c8, r8c9:
      Case A: color(r3c8) = color(r8c9). Identify.
        2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r8c3, r8c5, r9c5, r9c2}:
            Diagonals: {r8c3, r9c5} and {r8c5, r9c2} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r8c3) = color(r9c5) → forces r5c9 = r6c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r8c5) = color(r9c2) → forces r5c9 = r6c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r3c8) ≠ color(r8c9). Add edge.
        3.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r3c8, r6c8, r6c6, r7c6, r8c5, r8c9}
            Bridges: r9c8—r9c5 (edges r3c8—r6c8 ↔ r7c6—r8c5), r6c3—r8c3 (edges r6c8—r6c6 ↔ r8c5—r8c9), r3c6—r3c9 (edges r6c6—r7c6 ↔ r8c9—r3c8).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Bridges: r3c8—r6c8 (edges r3c6—r3c9 ↔ [r8c3=r9c8]—r6c3), r5c9—r6c8 (edges r3c9—r8c9 ↔ r6c3—r6c6), r8c5—r7c6 (edges r8c9—[r8c3=r9c8] ↔ r6c6—r3c6).
      Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r3c6, r9c9:
      Case A: color(r3c6) = color(r9c9). Identify.
        2.  Diamond {[r3c6=r9c9], r8c6, r8c7, r8c3} (spine r8c6—r8c7).
            → color([r3c6=r9c9]) = color(r8c3). Identify.
        3.  Odd wheel: hub [r3c6=r8c3=r9c9] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {r3c8, r3c9, r6c9, r6c3, r9c3, r9c4, r8c6, r8c7, r7c8} (length 9) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r3c6) ≠ color(r9c9). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r3c6, r3c9, r6c9, r6c3, r8c3, r8c6}
            Bridges: r9c9—r9c3 (edges r3c6—r3c9 ↔ r6c3—r8c3), r9c9—r8c7 (edges r3c9—r6c9 ↔ r8c3—r8c6), r6c5—r5c6 (edges r6c9—r6c3 ↔ r8c6—r3c6).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Satellites r3c6 (rung 1), r5c7 (rung 2) forced to distinct colors. Add edge.
  2.  Diamond {r5c7, r3c6, r5c6, r9c6} (spine r3c6—r5c6).
      → color(r5c7) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c8, r3c9, r7c9, r8c8}:
      Diagonals: {r3c8, r7c9} and {r3c9, r8c8} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r3c8) = color(r7c9) → forces r6c3 = r8c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r3c9) = color(r8c8) → forces r6c3 = r8c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  3.  Diamond {r3c8, r3c6, [r3c9=r6c7], [r6c5=r7c6]} (spine r3c6—[r3c9=r6c7]).
      → color(r3c8) = color([r6c5=r7c6]). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r8c3, r8c8, r9c8, r9c2}:
      Diagonals: {r8c3, r9c8} and {r8c8, r9c2} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r8c3) = color(r9c8) → forces [r3c8=r6c5=r7c6] = r9c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c8) = color(r9c2) → forces [r3c8=r6c5=r7c6] = r8c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r3c9) = color(r6c7). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c5, r8c5, r9c5, r7c6} (spine r8c5—r9c5).

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  4.  K₄ on {[r3c3=r6c6=r9c2], r7c5, r8c4, r9c6}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 3, row 6, row 8} − {col 3, col 6, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r6c8, r8c5, r8c8} = {r5c9, r7c9, r9c6}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  2.  Diamond {r5c9, r7c9, r9c6, r9c7} (spine r7c9—r9c6).
      → color(r5c9) = color(r9c7). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r5c9=r9c7], r8c8, r8c3, r9c2}:
      Diagonals: {[r5c9=r9c7], r8c3} and {r8c8, r9c2} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r5c9=r9c7]) = color(r8c3) → forces [r5c9=r9c7] = r6c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c8) = color(r9c2) → forces r6c3 = r6c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Satellites r6c3 (rung 1), r7c6 (rung 2), r5c9 (rung 3) forced to distinct colors. Add triangle.
  2.  Diamond {r6c8, r5c9, r6c3, r7c6} (spine r5c9—r6c3).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r6c3, r6c5, [r6c8=r7c6], r9c5} (spine r6c5—[r6c8=r7c6]).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c5). Identify.
  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c3=r9c5] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {[r6c8=r7c6], r8c6, r8c3, r9c2, r9c8} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Case A: color(r3c9) = color(r7c7). Identify.
        2.  Circular ladder {[r3c9=r7c7]—r7c3, r8c9—r8c2, r9c8—r9c2}:
            Satellites r3c3 (rung 1), r9c6 (rung 3) forced to distinct colors. Add edge.
        3.  Diamond {[r3c9=r7c7], r3c3, r3c6, r9c6} (spine r3c3—r3c6).
            → color([r3c9=r7c7]) = color(r9c6). Identify.
        4.  Odd wheel: hub [r3c9=r7c7=r9c6] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {r3c3, r3c6, r6c6, r6c7, r5c9, r8c9, r9c8, r9c2, r7c3} (length 9) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r3c9) ≠ color(r7c7). Add edge.
        5.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c8, r6c7, r7c7, r9c8}:
            Diagonals: {r5c8, r7c7} and {r6c7, r9c8} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c8) = color(r7c7) → forces r3c9 = r7c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r6c7) = color(r9c8) → forces r6c6 = r6c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {[r5c8=r6c2], r9c2, r9c8, r9c5} (spine r9c2—r9c8).
      → color([r5c8=r6c2]) = color(r9c5). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 6, row 9} − {col 8, col 9}.
      Remainder: {[r5c8=r6c2=r9c5], r9c2} = {r3c9, [r5c8=r6c2=r9c5], r8c9}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  4.  K₄ on {r3c9, [r5c8=r6c2=r9c5], r6c9, r8c9}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r6c8, r6c2, [r6c9=r9c8], r9c2} (spine r6c2—[r6c9=r9c8]).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r9c2). Identify.

  2.  Diamond {r6c8, r6c2, [r6c5=r9c6], r9c2} (spine r6c2—[r6c5=r9c6]).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r9c2). Identify.

      → color(r3c9) = color([r6c8=r9c2]). Identify.
  4.  Diamond {r3c3, r3c6, [r3c9=r6c8=r9c2], [r6c5=r9c6]} (spine r3c6—[r3c9=r6c8=r9c2]).
      → color(r3c3) = color([r6c5=r9c6]). Identify.
  5.  Odd wheel: hub [r3c3=r6c5=r9c6] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r3c6, [r3c9=r6c8=r9c2], r6c2, r5c3, r5c6} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

            row 9 {r9c2, r9c5, r9c9}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (box, box, box); row 6↔row 9 (col, col, box); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Case B: color(r2c9) ≠ color(r6c8). Add edge.
        3.  Diamond {r3c8, r2c9, r6c8, r5c9} (spine r2c9—r6c8).
            → color(r3c8) = color(r5c9). Identify.
        4.  Parity transport:
            row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, [r3c8=r5c9]}
            row 6 {r6c2, r6c5, r6c8}
            row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, r8c8}
            row 9 {r9c2, r9c5, r9c9}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (box, box, box); row 5↔row 8 (col, col, box); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □
